## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Bypass Audit

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in `envoyproxy/envoy` under `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/` and `source/common/tls/` that contain logic for certificate verification or validation. Specifically, identify files that reference `SSL_CTX_set_verify`, `X509_verify_cert`, `setCertificateValidationContext`, or `verify_mode`. Report which files handle server certificate validation vs client certificate validation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive audit of all C++ source files in Envoy v1.31.2 that handle TLS certificate validation. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

I've identified **17 core C++ source files** that contain certificate validation logic:

### **Server-Side Client Certificate Validation**
Files handling when a **server validates client certificates**:
- `source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.cc` - Uses `SSL_CTX_set_verify()` to configure client cert verification (line 528)
- `source/common/tls/server_context_impl.cc` - Calls `addClientValidationContext()` to enable client cert requirements (lines 147-149)

### **Client-Side Server Certificate Validation**
Files handling when a **client validates server certificates**:
- `source/common/tls/context_impl.cc` - Implements `customVerifyCallback()` that hooks verification (line 474) and `customVerifyCertChain()` (line 512)
- `source/common/tls/cert_validator/default_validator.cc` - Performs actual chain validation with `X509_verify_cert()` (line 315)
- `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.cc` - Alternative validator also calling `X509_verify_cert()` (line 177)

### **Key Validation Functions**
1. **`SSL_CTX_set_verify()`** - Sets OpenSSL verification mode for client certs
2. **`X509_verify_cert()`** - Performs the actual certificate chain validation
3. **`SSL_CTX_set_custom_verify()`** - Registers custom verification callback
4. **`customVerifyCallback()`** - Entry point for custom verification logic
5. **`addClientValidationContext()`** - Configures server-side client cert validation

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details on each file's role, the validation flow, and the call chain.
